TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- taichou: physical condition

Input: sensei shonichi taicho yokunatta genki aru to demo omoidasu memai ga kibun warukute taberarenakatta
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- deshouka: don't you think?

Input: konnichiha genki sou de naniyoridesune shuugou hisa wo mageyou to suru toki ni kowabari wo kanjimasu ka
Output: /no_think
```

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient.

Output: I have chest pain.

Output: I have no allergies.

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- deshouka: don't you think?

Input: kako ni ninen inai ni yuragu ka yakubutsu ya ihou yaku botsu wo shiyou shita mata ha chuushabari koto arimasu ka dearimasu
Output: /no_think
```

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- kangae: thinking

Input: shinkougan mashi da to kazeatari nannenkakou no houden kazeatari suru koto ha arimasu ka
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

#### LLM Output

> I feel like I have a fever, and I'm wondering if I should take cold medicine. Do you think I should take cold medicine?

### 12. `case-12-chronic-conditions` — History of chronic lung disease (asthma/COPD/pneumonia)

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient.

Output: I have chest pain.

Output: I have no allergies.

Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- iwai: congratulation

Input: wakatta sensei kore ijou kawaranai ranai to shinno desu ga sugi no youyaku itsu desuka saisho chichi no hi de happyoukai aru no de
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

#### LLM Output

> I understand, Sensei, but this won't change anymore. It's a diagnosis of cancer. However, the timing is too urgent because there's a celebration for my father's birthday on the first day.
